## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillations
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv/dt) is expressed as a function of velocity v and time t. Since position x is absent, the dynamics likely involve velocity-dependent nonlinear damping/restoring forces and possibly explicit time-dependent driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (simple viscous damping)
- Nonlinear (van der Pol-type) damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 + c2 * v**2) (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear damping with sinusoidal driving)
- Nonlinear damping with drive: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (van der Pol with driving)
- Quadratic velocity term: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 (quadratic nonlinearity in velocity)
- Polynomial velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity)
- Velocity with periodic modulation: dv_dt = c0 * v * cos(c1 * t) (parametrically modulated damping)
- Combined form: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (van der Pol driven oscillator)
- Rational velocity dependence: dv_dt = c0 * v / (1 + c1 * v**2) (saturating nonlinear damping)
- Sinusoidal restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v (position encoded through time)
- Power-law damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v)**c1 (generalized nonlinear drag)
- Full driven nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (comprehensive nonlinear driven oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power velocity terms (v, v**3, v**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation and indicate symmetric nonlinear damping
- Even-power velocity terms (v**2, v**4) break time-reversal symmetry and indicate asymmetric energy dissipation
- Product of velocity with its even powers, e.g., v*(1-v**2), indicates self-limiting amplitude (limit cycle behavior)
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- When position is absent, trigonometric functions of time may encode the implicit position dependence through x ~ sin(ωt)
- Negative linear velocity coefficient with positive cubic coefficient (c0*v + c1*v**3 with c0<0, c1>0) indicates energy pumping at small amplitudes and dissipation at large amplitudes
- Products of velocity and trigonometric functions of time v*sin(c*t) indicate parametric excitation or modulation
- Absence of constant (bias) terms indicates the system has zero mean acceleration over a cycle
